We cannot add anymore courses, and existing courses already have high content loads, so its a challenge to build in new (or very different) content. Lack of computational skills among students.  Despite repeated refernce to current students being digital natives, most students have no functional knowledge of computers or programs beyond their handful of favorite apps on their phone.  Its a constant source of surprise given how ubiquitous computers are in their live.  For example, many students have no idea what the difference is between the internet, an internet browser, a server, and other commonly used terms.  When the one thing they know how to do fails, many students have no idea how to work around it (e.., trying a different browser if an assigned activity doesnt work in their usual one).  I know that the students are capable of a lot, but the lack of experience and interest in anything computational is a large hurdle.   Many bioinformatics procedure are very button-click activities that allow students to follow directions without deeply thinking about material.  This is the part that I struggle with most in developing activities, because I want them to connect to the concepts were covering and not ust blindly report direct results (e.g., reporting an E-value without giving any thought to what that means biologically)." All of our BCB courses are cross-listed with either Biology & Biotechnology (BB), Computer Science (CS), or Mathematical Sciences (MA).  Some are offered as joint senior / grad level classes. CB 100X/BB 100X. EXPLORING BIOINFORMATICS AND COMPUTATIONAL BIOLOGYsCat. I.  Life scientists are generating huge amounts of data on many different scales, from DNA and protein sequence, to information on biological systems such as protein interaction netorks, brain circuitry, and ecosystems.  Analyzing these kinds of data requires quantitative knowledge and approaches using computer science and mathematics.  In this project-based course, students will use case studies to learn about both important biologcal problems and the computational tools and algorithms used to study them.  Students will study a sampling of topics in the field, including such areas as complex disease genetics, analysis of a flu epidemic, investigating antibiotic resistance, and undestanding the behavior of swarms, such as schooling fish.  Computational tools explored will include both freely-available web-based tools as well as guided programming using Python.sRecommended background: High school biology. Programming experience is nt required. BCB 3010 / BB 3010 SIMULATION IN BIOLOGYsCat II. Computer simulations are becoming increasingly important in understanding and predicting the behavior of a wide variety of biological systems, ranging from metastasis of cancer cells, to sprad of disease in an epidemic, to management of natural resources such as fisheries and forests.  In this course, students will learn to use a graphical programming language to simulate biological systems.  Most of the classroom time will be spent working ndividually or in groups, first learning the language, and then programming simulation projects. The concept learning process will be aided with many interesting experiments. It is a challenging course for the students who are new to this field. However, the overwhelming inventiveness and the beauty of construction of biological sytems will intrigue you and reward your efforts to understand the exciting story of Cell and Molecular Biology. The structure and function of cells will be discussed in relation to important cellular processes. Concepts to be covered include: the biology o macromolecules that the cells are made of (review), the technology for probing cell structure and function, membrane and organelle structure and function, topics on regulation of gene expression, signal transduction, cell division, cancer, and apoptosis.The experimental approaches that have lead to the current knowledge of cellular structure and function will be presented whenever possible. In addition, Bioinformatics, Genomics, and Proteomics which utilize computer science tools to study molecular bioloy, will also be introduced. In this course, students will learn about the major issues concerning representation, analysis and application of biological, molecula and biochemical information, especially from computational point of view. However, I think much thought needs to be put into adding/creating dedicated bioinformatics curriculum. Bioinformatics is still a rapidly developing field. It relies on the newest tecniques and knowledge in genetics, computer science, and statistics. Unfortunately my experience with dedicated bioinformatics curriculum has been that the bioinformatics courses are taught as a hodgepodge, containing many different disciplines that studens are never able to fully master. Many of the students I have worked with walk away feeling as though they are more aware of bioinformatics, but have not mastered any part of it. I feel that many students would be better served by completing a degree in cmputer science with a masters in biology, or vice versa. However, with a rigorous curriculum combining genetics, computer science, and statistics, I do believe it would be possible to create a core bioinformatics program."

However, many areas of modern biology are actually deeply quntitative and require preparation in math, statistics, and computer science. A major theme in bioinformatics is to integrate and understand biologica data generated by genome sequencing projects and other high-throughput molecular biology efforts. Bioinformatics tools are developed to reveal fundamental mechanisms underlying the structure and function of macromolecules, biochemical pathways, disease pocesses, and genome evolution  Although many bioinformatics problems are solved by computation and programming, this course itself does not require (practical) computer programming. However, it is expected that all of the students learn how to use the avalable bioinformatics software to solve biological problems. The aim is to emphasize critical thinking: understanding how these tools work in principle and developing a computational mind for biological problems. Major topics to be discussed in the course nclude: sequence analysis & algorithms, gene annotation, protein sequence analysis, proteomics, gene expression analysis, comparative genomics, genetic networks and pathways analysis, and systems biology. Biomedical BioinformaticssGenetics & Biochemisry Dept.sBioinformatics is a dynamic scientific discipline that utilizes computational and statistical methods for solving biological problems.  _Translational bioinformatics is an emerging discipline that bridges the gap between information stored n databases and application of this information to diagnosis, prognosis, and treatment of disease.  I have named this course Biomedical Bioinformatics because it sounds better! Many new students dont understand the computer  other than as a cluster of GUI icons that you slide around to do stuff which makes command lines and filesystems very difficult concepts. 3.  Department curriculum committees not seeing that scripting and HPC usage is a fundamental toolkit of biology thus not allotting credit hours to practical training.   For example, qPCR/PCR is a fundamental skill but RNAseq/GBS analysis is not."

Introduction to Bioinformatics: Entry level course for any life sciences student. Students learn basic Python and Linux, and are introduced to common databases. Students are also exposed to many different fieds within the Life Sciences in which a bioinformatics skill set is helpful. 2. Computational Biology: Covers major algorithms in bioinformatics. Students are expected to take five computer science classes before this course and are typically strong progrmmers. They code 20-30 different algorithms and learn the strengths/weaknesses of each, and finally they are asked to solve biological questions using their algorithms. 3. Bioinformatics: Capstone course for bioinformatics majors. Students are given dataat the start of the semester and asked to test some hypothesis using computational tools they develop, or download. The questions they are expected to address typically have not been solved, so these tend to be real projects and from time-to-time lead to ublications." With lab.s3. BI311: Biostatistics. Lectue course devoted to rigorous grounding in biological statistics, and in the application of statistical models to global health problems. Biostatistics is a lecture and hands-on course designed to provide students with the opportunity to develop statistica reasoning skills appropriate to analyze and implement biological experiments. Exemplars and case studies will be primarily derived from the public health field. Topics include principles of experimental design, sampling and variables, data categories andassumptions of parametric statistics, risk analysis, repeated measures, goodness of fit and contingency table analyses, and the general linear model.sBI420: Systems biology. This course will focus on the frontiers of our understanding of the multi-level ntworks that underlie biological systems. Lecture course reviewing the key concepts of the systems biology approach to ecological, organismal and cellular systems. Contribution of cornerstone technologies such as genomics, bioinformatics, proteomics and meabolomics will be reviewed, along with their computational foundations."	most of our students are premed.
